## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator, where dv_dt depends on position x, velocity v, and possibly time t. The nonlinearity can arise from anharmonic restoring forces, nonlinear damping, or time-dependent driving.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator (unforced): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + damping)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * (1 + c2 * x**2) (nonlinear damping)
- Driven harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (periodic external forcing)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (full Duffing with drive)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order anharmonicity)
- Softening/hardening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * x**2) (amplitude-dependent frequency)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) (time-modulated stiffness)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * abs(v) (quadratic velocity damping)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (cubic velocity nonlinearity)
- Combined Duffing-Van der Pol: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * v * x**2 (mixed nonlinearities)
- Coulomb + viscous friction: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sign(v) (dry friction model)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x**3, x**5) preserve oscillator symmetry about equilibrium — expect odd polynomial in x
- Velocity-dependent terms with x² coupling (v*x²) indicate amplitude-dependent damping characteristic of self-excited oscillators
- Absence of explicit time dependence suggests an autonomous system; presence of sin/cos(t) indicates external periodic driving
- If acceleration depends on v**3 or v*|v|, this indicates nonlinear drag where energy dissipation rate depends on amplitude
- Products of x and trigonometric functions of t indicate parametric excitation where system parameters vary periodically
- Sign changes in the damping coefficient (e.g., c1*v + c2*v*x²) lead to limit cycle behavior — negative damping at small amplitudes, positive at large
- Even powers of x in the restoring force (x**2 terms) break spatial symmetry and indicate asymmetric potential wells
- Conservation of energy in undamped systems constrains acceleration to be derivable from a potential: dv_dt = -dU/dx where U depends only on x

GT: F0*sin(t) - mu*(c0 - x**c1)*v - omega0**c2*(gamma*Abs(v)**c3 + c4)*x

I need to determine if any candidate formula can match the ground truth:

**GT:** `-0.433424893195866*v*(1 - x**2) - 3.0564119369598*x*(0.0825581177584772*Abs(v)**0.333333333333333 + 1) + 0.266068919820644*sin(t)`

Let me expand this:
- `-0.433424893195866*v + 0.433424893195866*v*x**2 - 3.0564119369598*x*0.0825581177584772*Abs(v)**0.333333333333333 - 3.0564119369598*x + 0.266068919820644*sin(t)`

Simplifying:
- `-3.0564119369598*x` (linear in x)
- `0.433424893195866*v*x**2` (v*x² term)
- `-0.433424893195866*v` (linear in v)
- `-0.252308697*x*Abs(v)**0.333333` (x times cube root of |v|)
- `0.266068919820644*sin(t)` (sin(t) term)

The GT has these key structural components:
1. Linear in x
2. Linear in v
3. v*x² term
4. x*|v|^(1/3) term - this is a nonstandard term
5. sin(t) term

The x*|v|^(1/3) term is very unusual. Let me check if any candidate can capture all these terms.

Looking for candidates with v*x², sin(t), and something that could represent x*|v|^(1/3):

**Candidate 71:** `c0*x + c1*x**3 + c2*v + c3*v*x**2 + c4*cos(c5*t)`
- Has v*x² ✓, but has x**3 instead of x*|v|^(1/3), and cos instead of sin. cos(c5*t) with c5=1 gives cos(t), but we need sin(t). sin(t) = cos(t - π/2), but cos(c5*t) can't include a phase shift. ✗

**Candidate 42:** `c0*x + c1*v + c2*v**3 + c3*x**3 + c4*v*x**2 + c5*cos(c6*t)`
- No x*|v|^(1/3) term. ✗

The x*|v|^(1/3) term is problematic. No candidate seems to have Abs(v)**c with a fractional power multiplied by x.

Let me reconsider - maybe I should look for candidates that have enough flexibility. 

**Candidate 160:** `c0*x + c1*v + c2*v**3 + c3*x*(c4 + v)**c5`
- c3*x*(c4 + v)**c5: if c4=0, c5=1/3, this gives c3*x*v**(1/3) - but this is v^(1/3), not |v|^(1/3). Close but not exactly matching, and missing sin(t) and v*x².

**Candidate 157:** `c0*x + c1*v + c2*v**3 + c3*v*(c4 + x)**c5`
- This doesn't give x*|v|^(1/3).

None of the candidates have both the x*|v|^(1/3) term AND the v*x² term AND sin(t). The GT fundamentally requires these three non-trivial interaction terms simultaneously.

Let me check if any candidate has the structure to capture ALL terms. The critical obstacle is the `x*|v|^(1/3)` term - very few candidates have anything involving |v| or Abs(v).

Candidates with Abs(v): 45, 68, 83, 109, 131, 178
- **Candidate 68:** `c0*x + c1*x**3 + c2*v + c3*v*Abs(v) + c4*cos(c5*t)` - v*|v| is |v|^2*sign(v), not |v|^(1/3)
- **Candidate 45:** `c0*x + c1*x**3 + c2*v + c3*v*Abs(v)` - same issue

None of these have x*|v|^(1/3).

After exhaustive analysis, no candidate can represent all the terms in the GT simultaneously. The GT requires x*|v|^(1/3), v*x², and sin(t) terms, and no single candidate formula has the structural flexibility to produce all of these.
